You are pretty damn ignorant on the subject of depression for someone who keeps eluding to the idea you suffer from it yourself. Instead of baiting for the cheap empathy you don't deserve, why not actually look into the subject? Clinical Depression is something that can be caused by a wide variety of things initially and affect people very differently. A huge part of this is physiology. The majority of clinical Depression is the result of hormonal production imbalance, once again caused by varying factors. This is why a majority of the symptoms are commonly associated with lethargic behavior, lack of emotional drive, etc. if you are not producing the correct amount of certain hormones for the variety of situations you find yourself in each day, you can suffer a lack of energy, feelings of resistance to activities including ones you typically enjoy, and similar. This can cause that sadness directly as a lack of motivation, accomplishment etc. feeds culturally into anxiety, confusion, self loathing, nihilistic perspectives etc. again, physiology is a complex and very individuated thing not only for a person but also that person in certain points of their life and based on what's occuring in their life. That is why medication treatment is not a solution for everyone now even some of the same people throughout their lives. You need different amounts of varying hormones to get you through the day so just supplementing extra so you have more than that amount doesn't work. Your body also tends to treat and react to artificially introduced chemicals differently than ones it produces itself so you have factors like building a natural resistance or resilience to it. This is where exercise can actually help. Exercising can actually cause an increase in development of these types of hormones so regular exercise is something that can potentially help individuals suffering from clinical depression. Unlike how you seem to think of it, it isn't just being inherently emo. It's not a personality thing but a medical thing that affects your personality. The shrinking aspect actually IS very accurate for a lot of people. You aren't just distracted from your depression you dimwitted bigot. Having friends support you can help because it stimulates the production of the kind of energy supplying hormones you may be deficient in but it depends on the person for a few factors. It's honestly really hypocritical of you to call out Big mouth when you yourself are spreading some really offensive and harmful misinformation on the subject. What can happen is the "weight" of it feel like it's lesser or shrinking based on a multitude of factors like greater production during certain periods, less triggers like anxiety, etc. Many people will go through valleys and peaks with their depression such as with seasonal or situation triggered low points. It's always there but with treatment and stabilization you can reduce the felt impact of it during periods of your life.

I feel like you don't understand Bigmouth in the slightest. The reason there are so many hormone monsters is because some people have different experiences with puberty, and the reason some of them have the same one is because they are going through generally the same thing. All the actors arent trying to sound like kids or not. All of them except Missy are just using their real voices. The reason they dont have a dramatic change at the end of the episode is because in real life you wouldnt either. Its a comedy. Things are going to be realistic and  over exaggerated. The reason people cant see the hormone monster/monsteress', is because its a metaphor for their hormones and emotions. Its really simple. Dont over think it. As a teenager it actually is relevant to me. Theres plenty of things in the show that dont make sense and dont have any reality behind them, because its a comedy. But there's also so much of the show that makes it realistic. Life dosent make sense sometimes. Especially when youre going through puberty. the whole show makes sense from the standpoint of someone who just wants to watch. Thats why so many people hate it. Because they go through the first 2/3 episodes and dont understand it.

The biggest problem with it can be explained by the laser pointer scene. In writing, a metaphor is a metaphor whether you've personified it or not, for the story to be cohesive and have a lesson that makes sense (since the set up for a lesson is already there) you must defeat it using something that relates to the actual problem the metaphor is meant to represent.  The issue is that they personified a metaphor in her mind and solved it in a way that would only work outside of her mind and would only work physically which is not really in line with how depression actually is whatsoever, it entirely ruins the stakes, not only for that episode, but for if they choose to ever do something similar to a different character

For the hormone monster not being exclusive for each kid, I think it's a metaphor of types of people, or groups even. You see when you go further into the history you have Maury who is absolutely crude, but semi-average and basic type of puberty 'for boys', Connie being the truly emotional and 100% 'girl energy', Mona who is absolutely openly all for being sexually active and try out all the possibilities or Rick who is the epitome of all the things wrong with hormones and with no possibility of change whatsoever. For me, they perfectly depict different types of personalities that ppl do depict and how they. Nothing makes sense, everything is 'just because'. And you must remember that because it's based of memories of the guys, some situations like, battling with depression, might be shown as a memory. Plus - puberty IS uncomfortable. It's disgusting, it's crass because you learn do's a don'ts, you smell because of the hormones, body odor and getting the hang of the hygene (pls don't tell me ALL of the teens are squeaky clean and always smell mint and flowers, because we all know it's not true), everything hurts because of growing pains, your body is changing and you in this weird twilight phase where some of your body parts are grown up and some are still kid like so you really often lack proportions and look like an alien. There was not one part in my body during puberty that I've liked- but not because of complexes or other social shit. I was in constant pain- if not from growing, then from periods. And the smell- let me tell you how absolutely my hormones DESTROYED every shirt I've owned, because of the sweat - at some point I just had to take soap, deodorant and at least 2 shirts, because it was so bad. And the list went on and on- it was absolutely horrible and I'm glad I'm in my adult body. To me the hormone monsters were clearly just anthropomorphized hormones/puberty/emotions, not a separate entity from the kids. The "rules" of the big mouth universe make complete sense when viewed this way rather than trying to force them in as a separate entity. Sure, the one kid made a meta joke once "there's a monster standing next to you" but everything else matches this explanation. Sometimes your hormones are visible, like for example if you have a fit of rage and bust a hole in a wall, sometimes they're internal and completely invisible when you're trying to hide them, sometimes you can't hide them no matter how hard you try. Puberty hormones make you do all sorts of nonsensical and regrettable things, and make you view the world in sometimes very dramatic and unrealistic ways. It actually makes for a very apt personification, it's that feeling of your hormones acting up and controlling you and feeling like it isn't really you, but actually it is, but it doesn't always feel like it, and sometimes you can control it and sometimes you can't, etc. Hell even the monsters sometimes being shared between the kids and sometimes not starts to make sense when viewed this way, many aspects and feelings of puberty feel the same between people and many don't and are unique.

2:30 Its perfectly fine to criticize a show, any show, and anyone can agree with that from an objective standpoint. Especially when its a show as objectively trashy and hard to sit through as Big Mouth. But what is not okay is to criticize something POORLY and use logical fallacies or incorrect arguments to critique it. For instance, most peoples critique of the Fiction Bible, BERSERK, (otherwise known as the most powerful and best work of art to ever grace the human species) usually comes from a place of purposeful ignorance, lack of understanding, or other forms of true voluntary incompetence in the highest regard. What I'm saying is, most people who dislike BERSERK are Stupid, or Chronically Online(AKA Stupid) Politically Motivated(AKA Stupid) or all of the above x10.  That being said, there are some genuine critiques of BERSERK, they just USUALLY aren't spoken of outside the fandom. See where I'm going here? A lot of people who critique shows like this, usually don't watch more than one episode before proudly proclaiming they can give an honest review, same thing with BERSERK. The folk who don't like it didn't actually read it because they know it as "The rape manga" or some other genuinely black-hearted slander.  Nobody is telling you that you cannot like something that is bad, plenty of people like Steven Universe and that show is propaganda trash to indoctrinate children into lesbian pedophilia (Hyperbole, but it really is pretty bad.) But when you say you don't like something genuinely good, even praised by MILLIONS of people as being the best fiction on earth, something objectively good, you usually find it hard to have a good reason to dislike it, that is for a good reason, its cause you are wrong you just can't admit it. You may dislike something about BERSERK, but chances are you didn't give it the time of day to actually see the parts you'd like, or you just don't like the genre as a whole and that in and of itself is a bad and close minded reason. It is perfectly okay though, and its also perfectly okay to hate something that is bad, like SU, like Big Mouth.  The biggest and most important thing is to just be honest, and preface that when you say you dislike something, its for illogical, bad, or personal reasons, and not anything reasonable.

19:33 Good job captions. Yes, it is just like church.
Speaking as someone who has no interest in Big Mouth whatsoever, when I hear people say "why did other, more deserving shows get cancelled when Big Mouth is still running?" What I hear is "I do not understand how other humans' minds work." I think a lot of people who say this are children, or people with the minds of children, who just assume that the things they like are objectively the best, as if the people who like other things must know that those things aren't as good and just... pretend to like them? And even more than that, executives who make programming decisions often haven't seen any of the shows they're making decisions about. They looking at ratings and viewership. A show that tons of people are watching, especially one that is critically-acclaimed and praised by its audiences, is going to stay on.  Even supposing the executives actually did feel the same way, that they agreed that Big Mouth was not as good as other shows, they can't ignore that more people watch and like it. If you're running a restaurant, and more people order the burger than the Wagyu steak, and you need to make budget cuts, you're not going to say "Well, we're discontinuing the burgers because Wagyu is superior," you're going to keep the thing that people are consuming. It's the same with shows. Executives don't say "I'm the big company boss, and I like this show because I'm stupid, so we're going to keep running it forever!" They make the popular choice. If you don't like that, your beef is with capitalism, not with people who don't "realize" your taste in shows is "objectively correct."  To be clear, this is not saying that public opinion is any measure of quality. A lot of low-effort garbage is beloved by the masses, but in a system like we have, viewership makes money, and profits are pretty much the only thing corporate decision-makers care about. At the same time, sometimes beloved, well-made media just isn't enjoyable for some people. It can be incredibly frustrating when things that you enjoy get cancelled in favor of things you find tiresome and dull, but it's not out of spite or to push some agenda. It's math. And not even complicated math. It's "big number is bigger than small number."

My main gripe is just the fact of how sexual it is while everyone in the show are minors. Yes it's a "coming of age story", but the only reason they oversexualized it isn't to be relatable, it's for shock humor. I'm not about policing content typically, so I don't think it should be banned, but I myself find it kinda unsettling, so therefore I don't watch it or support it, even though I think it can be funny occasionally. Idk, something about this show in particular feels off to me.
Not to say that there aren't tons of problems with the show, but I do feel this video doesn't quite understand it. Most of the stuff is metaphorical. That super-hero episode? It wasn't a 'what if', it was a kids interpretation of the events that actually happened. Even a lot of the rule breaking stuff, like that same kid seeing the hormone monster is just a meta joke. He's the only one that sees it (although that's of course abandoned later, too, but that is the joke, which is shown here twice as a sort of 'gotcha').  Aside from that, it's really not a coming of age story, and I think part of the problem is that the viewer here expects it to be one. It's not really about growing up, it's just about how awkward that period of life is.  As for the super ugly characters, I think there's also a good reason for that: They absolutely want the characters to look as non-sexy as possible, given the subject matter that they cover. The unappealing characters help them get away with nudity and things without it feeling pornographic.  Now, again, the show isn't great, and there are a million things wrong with it, but it does feel like a lot of the issues here are expecting the show to be something different from what it was meant to be, and treating that as a failure, and likewise kind of failing to read between the lines of the storytelling (and yes, I feel completely ridiculous implying that there's some inner depth to the ugly show with the gross sex jokes. It's not deep and complex, but it's far from a literal show).  Anyways, I think it's okay. Not great, by any stretch, but okay. It's different if nothing else.

I'm around 40 minutes in and I want to state my opinions on why I love Big Mouth.  The biggest thing with me is that my favorite genre is comedy and I like when things are pushed past society's comfort zones and show things that need to be talked about but not in a serious and in-depth way. Big mouth is a show that's not trying to be revolutionary with tackling puberty. It may have story arcs and progress from episode to episode but it's mainly a show where you can watch any episode in any order and still enjoy it. Like you said in the video, the artstyle seems gross but that's on purpose. The adults look better than the kids to exaggerate puberty which is the whole point of the show. Do the adults look stellar? No of course not but it's better to stand out even if ugly, than to go the safe route and imitate the artstyle of other shows and get forgotten because of it. Always found it odd when a voice actor gets replaced because of their race. I get it with stage/live actors as they have a physical onscreen presence so having the actors be right race for the role is important, but VAs don't have a physical presence. They just have to sound right, which means if a white dude can sound right, it's fine and the reverse is true. I don't remember anyone complaining Samurai Jack, a Japanese character, is voiced by Phil LeMarr, a black actor. Similarly Kratos in the rebooted God of War games isn't voiced by a Greek, he is voiced by Christopher Judge who is definitely not Greek. Both these examples are fine because their performances are excellent and highlight the greatest strength of voice acting as a profession: anyone can do it as long as they sound right for the part. Does the industry need more actors of colour? Yeah, absolutely. But that doesn't mean the talent you already have should be thrown out of the production because they weren't born with the right skin that the audience won't see anyway.

About the rules on seeing the monsters, I always kind of assumed that they were selectively invisible and could only be seen by who they want to be. They, especially Maury, but also the Monstress, are kind of like an embodiment of chaos and they push everyone to do different things and feel different ways. I also think the reason everyone has one of only a few monsters is for practicality. It already has a pretty big cast of characters and it would be an absolutely massive cast if every character had their own original monster to keep track of and remember who went with who. Having ambiguous rules for the fantasy makes it easier to follow the action without complicating things with 5 different characters all filling the same role and saying the same kinds of things but invisible to each other.

And no, I donâ€™t mean when they give valid criticisms that make sense, I mean when they get way too angry and worked up over mediocre writing. I understand getting angry over shows that are genuinely offensive or problematic, but a lot of the time I see this happen with shows that made the unfortunate mistake of not being a Godsend Shakespearean masterpiece. Instead of focusing on the positives of the show and discussing how disheartening it is that the show ended up having so many issues, people just automatically jump to calling it garbage. Itâ€™s rude to the people that did genuinely try to make good writing, but thatâ€™s not my main issue with it, seeing as writers should be prepared for backlash when making something this public. I think the real problem this creates is that it makes a hate bandwagon. It happened with Velma because people must have just gotten really angry from how obnoxious the titular main character is and the subsequent ranting made complaining about the show a trend. Going to be completely honest, I cannot get past the show's artstyle, it is fucking hideous. Thing is it's not like it's an issue I regularly have, I can watch South Park or ATHF perfectly fine. Big Mouth's artstyle though isn't just bad, I feel like it's almost purposely designed in a way to set off the revulsion centers in your brain. The only thing I can think of being worse is Problem Solverz, and that show looked so bad it was basically a cognitohazard.
When I was in middle school, I had pretty much no guidance or sense of comfort as I was raised in a conservative household. So when the show started and I watched it for the first time as an eighth grader, I felt like I could actually connect to what was going on. It didn't feel as if anyone else was going through any of that while I was, and it was a good source of entertainment for me. But as I got older, things made less sense and were less funny and MUCH more uncomfortable. At this point, it doesn't even feel like any of the struggles of the characters are real anymore. You can tell what the writers are trying to say, but it just doesn't work. It feels like random fluff just to keep the show going, and that sense of "yeah I went through this same thing" is gone. I can't connect with any of the characters anymore, and the season 6 finale was extremely disappointing. And there's so many annoying characters, such as the anxiety mosquitoes, coach Steve, and I have no clue what's going on with that baby hormone monster.  I'm glad that there's people out there who want to shine a light on the challenges middle schoolers go through during puberty. It may even help them feel less alone and more understood, like young me. But now the show is this big bundle of weird humor and unlikable characters. Like wtf is even going on with Andrew?? I think the show should've stopped much earlier (maybe after season 3 or 4) because now it feels like they're beating a dead horse when there's much better adult animation they could work on, like Inside Job!  I still watch Big Mouth, as it can be entertaining sometimes. Despite not being connected to anything about it anymore and being very confused about several things going on in the show, it's still watchable.  But that's just my opinion on the show, I agree with a lot of what you said in this video if not all of it! Thank you for covering this. :)

Hey, I work in the industry and wanna give you all some insight into what animation workers think because you're all very uninformed. Whenever a show gets canceled, almost no one turns around and says "oh but why does X show still get renewed". Why? because ANY show on the air means jobs. In an industry where studios seem to be hell-bent on axing every animated show, any potential landing spot for artists/ workers is good news. I'm sure some of the artists affected by the inside Job cancellation may very well find work on Big Mouth. I can see the frustration on the audience side, but if you truly want to see more animation it's important to support ALL animation for the sake of the workers, instead of just your personal favs. A rising tide lifts all boats.

With some places getting updated curriculum way later than they should, or even getting it reverted back to an older, out of date model. There's an inherent value to this show, even if by design it makes some people uncomfortable. It isn't doing that to be edgy or meta, it's just the nature of the topics they deal with.

Everyone gives all the credit for how great the show was to Stephen Hillenburg (partially out of sentimentality and remembrance, I'm sure), and while yes, he was definitely an important asset to the show and it gradually got way worse after he stepped down... he only wrote about three episodes of the show, and they were all VERY early on.
I think Big Mouth is actually pretty decent. There's a lot going on with it. I think it's obnoxious and far too on the nose, but it's real world problems covered by the facade of dark humor.

Big Mouth is very strange in that it doesn't seem to have or know its audience or demographic. I know for a fact that Big Mouth is popular among tweens and teens because everyone around me is watching the new season whenever they come out. Big Mouth is oddly structured like a show for children, with very ham-fisted messages, and most having complex concepts be personified such as with how it does the whole Hormone Monster thing. But where Big Mouth started to lose me was with its 3rd and 4th season. The first 2 were admittedly crude, but ultimately harmless, but by the 3rd I genuinely think the writers of the show had let the critical acclaim get to their head and got dangerously lazy. It was from this season where EVERY emotion the characters felt had to have some metaphorical equivalent and it went off the rails quickly, "Love Bug" "Anxiety Mosquitoes", someone else put it best, this lead to the season finale where they defeated anxiety with the "Gratitode" and the way it just simplified the struggle with anxiety was horrible  ; "Big Mouth is a show that thinks that it's smart because it uses metaphors and metaphors are for smart people". I honestly agree, the show from the 3rd season downwards because more and more of the same personification nonsense and it got worse when it began to rely more and more on Meta humour and references and over indulgent soap box nonsense.  Yet there are people who genuinely love this show, and that's fine. I keep watching because it always comes out when there's nothing else to watch on Netflix and I genuinely hate the show but I am enamoured by how awful I find it.
